title: "HELP! Playing TV in Myth crashes X"

### Post by pssturges on 2007-11-08
Hi,

My main Myth frontend/backend machine was working nicely with my GF6200, but with the new ATI drivers out I thought I'd give my x1300 a try:oops:. That wasn't a success so I went back to my 6200.  Un-installed the ATI drivers and re-installed the nvidia drivers via the restricted drivers manager. 

Most things are actually working fine, even compiz. However, when I try to play video (TV) in myth, xserver crashes and flicks me back to the login screen:shock: I have tried re-installing the drivers via restricted drivers manager and also envy, but with no luck.

Also when I start nvidia-settings I get the output shown in the attached screen shot::confused:

I run 'sudo nvidia-xconfig' as suggested and it seems to update my xorg.conf successfully. Reboot, but still no fix!

I suspect that either a critical package has gone missing or some remnant of ATI driver is causing a conflict, but I have no idea where to start.

This machine is used for my family's main tv viewing, so I'm pretty desperate to fix this quick!

Below is my xorg.conf. Let me know if any further info is needed.

Thanks in advance for any help

Phil

### Post by newlinux on 2007-11-09
Have you looked at your logs for clues as to what is happening?

/var/log/Xorg.log.0 would be the most recent Xorg log. Maybe post that.

First thing I notice is that your xorg.conf file is using the open source nv driver, not the nvidia restricted driver. Try changing "nv" to "nvidia" e.g.:

```
Section "Device"
	Identifier	"nVidia Corporation NV44 [GeForce 6200 TurboCache(TM)]"
	Driver		"nv"
	BusID		"PCI:2:0:0"
EndSection
```

should be:

```
Section "Device"
	Identifier	"nVidia Corporation NV44 [GeForce 6200 TurboCache(TM)]"
	Driver		"nvidia"
	BusID		"PCI:2:0:0"
EndSection
```

If you have nvidia binaries installed. Then restart your x-server.

---

### Post by newlinux on 2007-11-09
Oh you don't need to reboot to restart your X-server. doing a ctrl-alt-backspace should restart it. If nvidia is running, based on your xorg.conf you should see a little nvidia logo before gdm loads.

---

### Post by newlinux on 2007-11-10
Well, I'm not sure what else to try. Can do a whole bunch of diagnostics. You should run mythfrontend from a terminal with the -v playback switch, and output it to a log file.

So something like:

```
mythfrontend -v playback &> mythfrontend_log
```

To get the output of mythfrontend right before it crashes X. Then when you restart X you can look at what happened with mythfrontend.

You might also want to look at your backend logs located at:

/var/log/mythtv/mythbackend.log

and syslog for clues about the crash:

/var/log/syslog

Also, try playing a recording file that crashes in myth with mplayer and see if it crashes. This might help determine if it is a myth specific problem. 

Also what processor are you using, what tuner card, what types of recordings (digital, analog, SDTV, HDTV). What playback settings (deinterlace filter, xvmc, etc.).

Hopefully we can gleam a clue from some of this info.

---

### Post by pssturges on 2007-11-10
Hi,
First of all newlinux I really do appreciate your time and effort in helping me get this sorted out.

This machine is an athlon 64x2 4600+, Asus M2n mobo, 1gb ddr2. The recordings are from a DVICO DVB-T card. Some HD, some SD PAL. Audio is generally ac3 which i passthrough via coax spdif to my amp. I have 2 other frontend machines that connect to this backend and they work fine. I use the standard decoder with de-interlace set to kernel.

So an update as to how things are gong. The recodings play fine in mplayer when in a window, however mplayer crashes (not xserver) when I switch to full screen. Myth I use at full screen also.

Here's my ouput from myth fronted:

---

### Post by newlinux on 2007-11-11
Looking at these, I don't see anything that is causing the problem. sorry I couldn't be more helpful. It appears to be a myth problem. My only suggestion would be to try changing the playback settings in the setup menu and see if something works (turn off/on deinterlacing, us different filters, turn off/on OpenGL, and the other options). Maybe someone else will come along and know what the problem is.

Definitely seems to be with myth, or myth's interaction with Xorg, due to mplayer playing it right. Maybe even try a different window manager/desktop environment. Make sure to try it with compiz turned off...

---
